GEOTECHNICAL ENGINEERING CONSTRUCTION OBSERVATION
SOIL NAIL INSTALLATION AND TESTING
KAPOLEI INTERCHANGE COMPLEX PHASE 2
Dear Mr Barre
This letter report summarizes our geotechnical observation services performed
during the installation and testing of the pre production sacrificial and production soil
nails for the Kapolei Interchange Complex Phase 2 project located in the Ewa area on
the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project location and general vicinity are shown on the
Project Location Map Plate 1
In general this letter report presents our observations and the results of the soil
nail installation and testing performed on the soil nails for the project from
March 16 2016 through was the general
contractor for the project and Prometheus Construction was the specialty subcontractor
responsible for installation and testing of the soil nails
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
The Kapolei Interchange Complex Phase 2 project consists of a new
interchange north mauka of Kamokila Boulevard in the Ewa area on the Island of
Oahu Hawaii The interchange will involve the extension of Wakea Street over and
across the Interstate Route H 1 Highway towards the existing Wet n Wild Hawaii
Amusement Park A cut slope with a height of about 38 feet is planned at the mauka
side of Ramp KA 1 from about 25 to 31 25 A soil nailed slope system
was designed to minimize the amount of right of way needed for the new cut slope
Wilson Okamoto Corporation
Page 2
W O 5537 70 B
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Geolabs Inc conducted a geotechnical engineering exploration of the project
site and our recommendations are presented in the report entitled Geotechnical
Engineering Exploration Kapolei Interchange Complex Phase Hawaii
dated The purpose of our geotechnical engineering services during
construction of the project was to observe the construction and testing of the soil nails
for general conformance with the project plans and specifications
SOIL NAIL INSTALLATION AND TESTING
As part of the project requirements a reinforced shotcrete soil nail slope system
was designed consisting of 83 individual reinforcing bars grouted into drilled holes to
stabilize the existing slope A structural shotcrete layer was specified to be placed on the
face of the wall in addition to an architectural sculpture shotcrete layer for aesthetic
appearance
A 3 inch thick fiber reinforced shotcrete facing was constructed in front of the face of
the wall prior to the soil nail installation This fiber reinforced shotcrete facing was
constructed to provide a level working surface for drilling and testing of the soil nails
The soil nail installations verification and proof tests were performed by
Prometheus Construction The approximate locations of the soil nails are shown on the Soil
Nail Location Plan Plate 2 Installation and testing of the soil nails were conducted from
March 16 2016 to A summary of the soil nail installations and testing are
presented on Plates 3 1 through 3 4
Soil Nail Installation
A Geolabs representative observed the drilling and grouting operations during
construction of the soil nails The soil nails were drilled using a TEI Platform Rock Drill
mounted on a LC excavator The TEI drill rig was equipped with a down
the hole hammer and an 8 inch underreammer percussion bit
The soil nail holes were drilled to depths between 10 and 22 2 feet from the front
face of the fiber reinforced shotcrete facing with an inclination about 15 degrees from
perpendicular to the shotcrete facing An 8 Inch OD temporary steel casing was installed to
depths between about 2 5 and 13 8 feet behind the existing shotcrete facing to maintain
stability of the drilled hole After the hole was drilled to the specified depth the temporary
casing was removed and the Grade 75 10 threaded bar was inserted into the drilled hole
Centralizers were placed along the threaded bar at 5 foot intervals For the nails that were
selected for testing purpose the top 3 feet of the threaded bar was covered with a PVC
pipe to create an unbonded section
A 1½ inch diameter high density plastic grouting tube was inserted into the drilled
hole along the soil nail tendon Grouting began progressively from the bottom to top
through the grouting tube until fresh grout appeared at the top of the hole The grouting
Wilson Okamoto Corporation
Page 3
W O 5537 70 B
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
tube was removed after completion of the grouting operation The grout was designed with
a minimum 28 day compressive strength of 4 000 psi
The soil nails were designed as 8 inch diameter nails however Prometheus
Construction used a 6 inch diameter drill bit for the verification soil nails i e T1 and T2
and accepted the risk of the soil nail failing the verification testing Soil Nails T 1 and T 2
were not able to withstand the design loads therefore the contractor was required to install
8 inch diameter Soil Nails T 1A and T 2A for the replacement verification tests
The original plan was to install 83 soil nails Due to the existing ground condition
Soil Nail No 8F was added to the plan During installation of the second row of nails for
Column Nos 4 to 6 caving in of the borehole was encountered due to the existing fill
material on the upper portion of the slope It was recommended that the top row production
nail and 6F be omitted Soil Nail No 1 A1 also was omitted due to the
presence of man made obstructions behind the slope Logs of the individual soil nails
recording our observations and other pertinent information by our representative for each
soil nail installed are provided in the Soil Nail Installation Records Plates through
Soil Nail Testing
In accordance with the project specifications the verification soil nails shall be
loaded to 200 percent of the design load 44 0 kips and held for 60 minutes at 150 percent
of the design load 33 0 kips Based on the project specifications 10 percent of the
production nails eight nails were selected for proof testing Production test nails have at
least 3 feet of unbonded test length Proof test nails were loaded to 150 percent of the
design load 33 0 kips At this point the load was maintained for 60 minute to measure the
creep movements The criteria for acceptance of the soil nails consist of the following
For the verification tests a total creep movement of less than 0 08 inches
per log cycle of time between the 6 and 60 minute readings is measured
during creep testing and the creep rate is linear or decreasing throughout
the creep test load hold period
For the proof tests a total creep movement of less than 0 04 inch is
measured between the 1 and 10 minute readings or a total creep
movement of less than 0 08 inch is measured between the 6 and
60 minute readings and the creep rate is linear or decreasing throughout
the creep test load hold period
Total measured movement at the maximum test load exceeds 80 percent
of the theoretical elastic elongation of the test nail unbonded length
Pullout failure does not occur at the maximum test load
Wilson Okamoto Corporation
Page 4
W O 5537 70 B
GEOLABS INC

In accordance with the project specifications verification tests were performed on
Soil Nails T 1 and T 2 on March 21 2016 Equipment failure occurred during the testing of
Soil Nail T 1 between the 125 percent 27 5 kips and 150 percent 33 0 kips loading The
soil nail was retested on March 22 2016 Subsequently the test nail was unable to obtain
the test load of 43 5 kips without additional movement The locations of verification test
nails are shown on Plate 2
Soil Nail T 2 was loaded to the maximum test load of about 44 0 kips 200 percent
of the design load The head movement for the soil nail at each load increment up to the
maximum test load was measured and recorded After testing the soil nail to 200 percent of
the design load the dial gages were removed from the set up and the soil nail was loaded
until failure The soil nail loading was terminated at about 333 percent of the design load
73 3 kips due to bending of the testing frame
The 6 inch diameter Soil Nail T 1 did not provide enough capacity to withstand the
test load The contractor re installed two 8 inch diameter nails for a new set of verification
testing The installation of Test Nails T 1A and T 2A was completed on and
pullout tests were performed on April 11 and 12 2016 Soil Nail T 1A was loaded to the
maximum test load of about 44 0 kips 200 percent of the design load The head movement
for the soil nail at each load increment up to the maximum test load was measured and
recorded After testing the soil nail to 200 percent of the design load the test nail was
unloaded in four load decrements Total measured head movement at 200 percent of the
design load was about 0 21 inches
Soil Nail T 2A was also loaded to the maximum test load of about 44 0 kips
200 percent of the design load Total measured head movement at 200 percent of the
design load was about 0 1 inches Results of the verification tests including Load versus
Displacement and the Creep Movement versus Time curves are presented on Plates
through
In accordance with the project specifications proof tests on selected production
nails were performed on Soil Nails 14E and 9F on
and Maximum total head movement was about 0 264 inches
for Soil Nail 5C Results of the proof tests including Load versus Displacement and the
Based on our observations we believe that the soil nails observed by Geolabs have
been installed in general conformance with the project plans and specifications and within
the limits of generally accepted construction practices Based on our observations of the
soil nail tests performed by the contractor it is our professional opinion that the soil nails
have been installed to provide sufficient load capacity with tolerable movements
Wilson Okamoto Corporation Page 5
W O 5537 70 B
LIMITATIONS
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site therefore some of the work for the soil
nail installation and testing may have occurred without our direct observation However
we believe that the level of geotechnical observation provided is reasonable in reducing
the geotechnical risks to the project
Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of
geotechnical engineering practice no warranty is expressed or implied Provision of
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance nor does it guarantee construction
of any type The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of their work for
adhering to the plans and specifications and for repairing defects regardless of when they
are found
CLOSURE
We appreciate the opportunity to provide geotechnical engineering services to
Wilson Okamoto Corporation on this project If you have questions or need additional
information please contact our office
Respectfully submitted

A total of about 0 25 bags of cement 0 3 cubic feet were used to prime the system
A total of about 7 75 bags of cement 8 9 cubic feet were used to grout
Tremie pipe was removed at end of grouting
Grout Take takes into account the void at the top of the nail due to inclination and the volume of the rebar
CG 500 series ChemGrout grout plant was used to mix grout with high shearing action
The contractor began batching the grout at 13 40PM
Grout was placed thru a 1 2 diameter high density plastic tremie pipe
Tremie pipe was inserted into the lowest point of the drilled hole and hole was grouted from bottom up
Grouting was terminated when sound grout returned at top of hole
Grout cubes were cast by Consolidated Testing

Grout used was from the batch made for soil nail T 1A
A total of about 4 5 bags of cement 5 2 cubic feet were used to grout
Tremie pipe was removed at end of grouting
Grout Take takes into account the void at the top of the nail due to inclination and the volume of the rebar
CG 500 series ChemGrout grout plant was used to mix grout with high shearing action
The contractor began batching the grout at 12 50PM
Grout was placed thru a 1 2 diameter high density plastic tremie pipe
Tremie pipe was inserted into the lowest point of the drilled hole and hole was grouted from bottom up
Grouting was terminated when sound grout returned at top of hole
Grout cubes were cast by Consolidated Testing

Remarks
CG 500 series ChemGrout grout plant was used to mix grout with high shearing action
Grout was placed thru a 1 2 diameter high density plastic tremie pipe

CG 500 series ChemGrout grout plant was used to mix grout with high shearing action
Grout was placed thru a 1 2 diameter high density plastic tremie pipe
Grout cubes were cast by Consolidated Testing
Tremie pipe was removed at end of grouting
Grout Take takes into account the void at the top of the nail due to inclination and the volume of the rebar
A total of about 8 bags of cement 9 2 cubic feet were used to grout

Grouting was terminated when sound grout returned at top of hole

Remarks
CG 500 series ChemGrout grout plant was used to mix grout with high shearing action
Grout was placed thru a 1 2 diameter high density plastic tremie pipe
Grout cubes were cast by Consolidated Testing
Tremie pipe was removed at end of grouting
Grout Take takes into account the void at the top of the nail due to inclination and the volume of the rebar
A total of about 3 6 bags of cement 4 1 cubic feet were used to grout
